<span id="freeTextContainer14057261776885797438">A fun little trip through Greek Mythology with furry little Pan as the hero of the story.<br />Simply brain candy and although I enjoyed this book, I would not recommend it for children ...<br />waaay too much ... ummmm ... romping with the maenads. ;)</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_1243983240">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1243983240" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/3220846-angela-kidd-shinozaki" class="left imgcol" title="Angela Kidd Shinozaki"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1270926582p2/3220846.jpg" alt="Angela Kidd Shinozaki" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1243983240?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Apr 02, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/3220846-angela-kidd-shinozaki" class="user" title="Angela Kidd Shinozaki">Angela Kidd Shinozaki</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/59389.The_Great_God_Pan" title="Paperback 9780440229254" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1243983240">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2068451534180249681">I thought this book would be fun--a lighthearted romp--for spring. The main problem is that it doesn't get going until chapter 10 The Prophecy on page 88, and it's only 150 pages. So I would suggest skimming the first sections. The only important part is the scene where he meets Iphigenia-- his love interest. I think what the author is trying to do is set up the character of Pan that we know and love. The one that likes to frolic with maidens in nature, which is fine, but it goes on for too many</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText2068451534180249681">I thought this book would be fun--a lighthearted romp--for spring. The main problem is that it doesn't get going until chapter 10 The Prophecy on page 88, and it's only 150 pages. So I would suggest skimming the first sections. The only important part is the scene where he meets Iphigenia-- his love interest. I think what the author is trying to do is set up the character of Pan that we know and love. The one that likes to frolic with maidens in nature, which is fine, but it goes on for too many pages without a clear plot. The other issue is that there are a lot of digressions about the other gods and the myths and stories surrounding them, which don't really relate to the story. They're unnecessary and slow the reading down tremendously. <br />But what makes this read ultimately satisfying is the change we see take place in Pan. He becomes much more dynamic and relatable by the end of the book. I dare say we come to care for him--worrying about his fate--and even admire him. The ending will stay with you for a long time. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="2068451534180249681">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer4338615382319825443">I stumbled across this book while looking for some new pictures to post of my beloved satyr god.   <span style="display:none" id="freeText4338615382319825443">I stumbled across this book while looking for some new pictures to post of my beloved satyr god. It wasn't a purchase I regret.<br /><br />The story is absolutely beautiful even if there are minor contradictions to the actual mythology. It tells the story of Pan's love for Iphigenia.<br /><br />Told through Pan's eyes, the reader is shown how many of the most notable events in the Great God's life came to happen, which will give lovers and followers of our carefree god, a new look at him and a much deeper understanding about who he is.<br /><br />The story nearly broke my heart, but it is a story I will read over and over again.<br /><br />I would recommend this book to any lover of Mythology, any follower of Pan, and any lover of true love.<br /><br />I give this book 5 of 5 pentacles</span>

        rated it

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer69923308">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13352649357624664615">Donna Jo Napoli's The Great God Pan is the tale of young half Olympian god, half goat Pan. Pan is greatly adored by all creatures and gods of Olympus, but he is forever burdened by a curse put on him by the goddess of love, Aphrodite to be unloveable after his father Hermes forced her into bed with him. Pan is disturbed by this as well as his inability to be either completely god or completely goat throughout the book causing him to be caught in between two different worlds never knowing where h</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText13352649357624664615">Donna Jo Napoli's The Great God Pan is the tale of young half Olympian god, half goat Pan. Pan is greatly adored by all creatures and gods of Olympus, but he is forever burdened by a curse put on him by the goddess of love, Aphrodite to be unloveable after his father Hermes forced her into bed with him. Pan is disturbed by this as well as his inability to be either completely god or completely goat throughout the book causing him to be caught in between two different worlds never knowing where he truly belong. Although not a work of literary genius, The Great God Pan is a good read for anyone looking for a short, yet entertaining book with a solid plot line, easy to understand language, interesting story, and strong emotion. The strong emotion is especially apparent when Pan falls in love with Iphigenia, daughter of King Agememmnon and Queen Clydemnystra. The cartoon-like picture on the cover of the book and first few pages led me to think it had the potential to be somewhat boring and uneventful, but after just a few more pages I realized that would not be the case. Overall, I really enjoyed this book and would recomment it to almost anyone. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="13352649357624664615">...more</a>

        rated it

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,

              <span style="display:none" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer123656586">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10134690066215837130"> The great god pan is read more like a short story than a novel. It is very easy reading and i imagine would be a great way to wean kids onto classical Greek mythology and legend. The story follows Pan, son of Helios (god of the sun), and goat/god hybrid he lives out his days running through the forest of the Mediterranean playing with goats and other animals, shying away from humans, getting teased by sexy nymphs that want only to ridicule, and visiting assorted gods as he makes his way through</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText10134690066215837130">	The great god pan is read more like a short story than a novel. It is very easy reading and i imagine would be a great way to wean kids onto classical Greek mythology and legend. The story follows Pan, son of Helios (god of the sun), and goat/god hybrid he lives out his days running through the forest of the Mediterranean playing with goats and other animals, shying away from humans, getting teased by sexy nymphs that want only to ridicule, and visiting assorted gods as he makes his way through the countryside. He has virtually no contact with humans because they are scared of him; however he is loved by all the gods. Deep down though he feels that he is different from the others. He can turn neither full god or full goat and as such after many mistreatments begins to feel that he belongs nowhere. That the gods that he had enjoyed the company of saw him only as a pet. So he goes into exile having only occasional meetings with Iphigenia the only human girl to ever receive him as an equal and gods that truly loved him. Until he accepts himself and thanks eternaly the human that saw throught his outer appearence and recognized the person he was. It is an inspiring little tale of self identification and love for anyone to enjoy on some level.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer7781061189352556577">I love Greek mythology and when I found out that one of my required authors for class had written one, AND it was young adult fiction, I just HAD to read it. I was pleasantly surprised with this one too. It gives the story of the gap in Pan's myth. He's the only god to have "died" and Napoli wanted to know why, so she wrote the story herself. It's very "Greek" in the sense that you have to understand it is written as a Greek myth and not as a normal novel. If you have read other Greek myths thou</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText7781061189352556577">I love Greek mythology and when I found out that one of my required authors for class had written one, AND it was young adult fiction, I just HAD to read it. I was pleasantly surprised with this one too. It gives the story of the gap in Pan's myth. He's the only god to have "died" and Napoli wanted to know why, so she wrote the story herself. It's very "Greek" in the sense that you have to understand it is written as a Greek myth and not as a normal novel. If you have read other Greek myths though, it will be easy for you to understand.<br /><br />I think this book is a great way to get young adults interested in Greek mythology. It's a quick read, and its not too wordy, or full of too much history, which oftentimes bores young adults if they attempt to read something along the lines of Homer's Odyssey. <br /><br />Drugs: None<br />Sex: maybe there is, but its very well hidden if there is.<br />Alcohol: some wine, I mean his uncle is the GOD of wine...<br />Language: None<br />Violence: some death</span>

  <a href="/user/show/6627881-emma" class="left imgcol" title="Emma"><img src="http://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" alt="Emma" /></a>

      <a href="/user/show/6627881-emma" class="user" title="Emma">Emma</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/59389.The_Great_God_Pan" title="Paperback 9780440229254" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/6627881-emma?shelf=donna-jo-napoli" class="actionLinkLite">donna-jo-napoli</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/6627881-emma?shelf=fairy-tale" class="actionLinkLite">fairy-tale</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/6627881-emma?shelf=mythology" class="actionLinkLite">mythology</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/6627881-emma?shelf=my-favorites" class="actionLinkLite">my-favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer226645836">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2017824987092385757"> The Great God Pan, by Donna Jo Napoli, is yet another beautifully written story of love and loss. Though it is short, it succeeds in conveying everything that could be wished. The Great God Pan is an interpretation of the Greek myths surrounding Pan, the god of nature. Pan is the son of Hermes and a goat, and is therefore stuck between two worlds, not really fitting into either. The book starts with a visit from his father, and continues on to Pan's meeting with a beautiful princess. Dealing wi</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText2017824987092385757"> The Great God Pan, by Donna Jo Napoli, is yet another beautifully written story of love and loss. Though it is short, it succeeds in conveying everything that could be wished. The Great God Pan is an interpretation of the Greek myths surrounding Pan, the god of nature. Pan is the son of Hermes and a goat, and is therefore stuck between two worlds, not really fitting into either. The book starts with a visit from his father, and continues on to Pan's meeting with a beautiful princess. Dealing with his feelings for her and the impossibility that she could love someone like him, Pan sets off around Greece learning things. The book ends with Pan making the choice between leaving the space between two worlds, or abandoning his love. This book talks of love, heartbreak, and growing up. Combining a love story and Greek mythology, this book is perfect for anyone who loves Donna Jo Napoli or anyone who enjoys Greek mythology.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="2017824987092385757">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/428733907?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Nov 22, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/3846743-althea-ann" class="user" title="Althea Ann">Althea Ann</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/59389.The_Great_God_Pan" title="Paperback 9780440229254" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer428733907">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17036898760302906391">I can get very particular about my favorite gods, so if you're going to do one on Pan, Dionysus (or Loki), I'm gonna be exacting, sorry.<br /><br />It's also an odd choice of title: in the afterword, Napoli explains that her choice of title is based on a line from Plutarch's 'Moralia,' but she cannot be unaware that there is already a very famous story by Arthur Machen with the same title.<br /><br />Anyway, I've read several of Napoli's mythology and folklore-inspired books, and generally like them, but this is not th</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText17036898760302906391">I can get very particular about my favorite gods, so if you're going to do one on Pan, Dionysus (or Loki), I'm gonna be exacting, sorry.<br /><br />It's also an odd choice of title: in the afterword, Napoli explains that her choice of title is based on a line from Plutarch's 'Moralia,' but she cannot be unaware that there is already a very famous story by Arthur Machen with the same title.<br /><br />Anyway, I've read several of Napoli's mythology and folklore-inspired books, and generally like them, but this is not the best I've read. It's not bad, but it doesn't really capture the wildness, ecstasy and divinity of Pan. Admittedly, the fact that the book is marketed at teen readers may put a bit of a crimp in things, but I felt that still, it could have been done better. It does a good job of working various aspects of the mythology into a story; but Napoli's Pan, as a character, is a little bit immature, pathetic and annoying. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="17036898760302906391">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_189081994">

  <div class="left bodycol">

          added it


          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/1012517.The_Great_God_Pan" title="Library Binding 9780385901208" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer189081994">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer567524417733211066">2004- I've read some of the author's other retellings and was a bit disappointed with this one. We meet Pan, the half goat/half god who basically flits around the woods with other mythical creatures all day. It isn't until he meets Iphigenia and falls in love with her that his life really seems to have a purpose. People with any background in Greek mythology know that Pan had a curse placed on him upon birth that he will never be loved in return. His quest to find Iphigenia again then seems a bi</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText567524417733211066">2004- I've read some of the author's other retellings and was a bit disappointed with this one. We meet Pan, the half goat/half god who basically flits around the woods with other mythical creatures all day. It isn't until he meets Iphigenia and falls in love with her that his life really seems to have a purpose. People with any background in Greek mythology know that Pan had a curse placed on him upon birth that he will never be loved in return. His quest to find Iphigenia again then seems a bit fruitless to the reader, but what we don't realize is that he may be able to save her from her father's mission to sacrifice her. This book needed more detail. I felt it was lacking in some other areas as well, as the plot meandered quite a bit. I did like how the author included a family tree at the beginning so we understood how everyone was related however.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="567524417733211066">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <a href="/review/list/1323157-keith?shelf=thelema" class="actionLinkLite">thelema</a>,

          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer27089346">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10362193172540232012">A bit of a tear-jerker, a bit of an Olympian love story, both of which should be obvious to anyone who already knows the related myths or the Greeks' penchant for classical tragedy. Napoli weaves a number of interrelated mytic stories into the tapestry, and in the process creates quite a plausible fill for two of the gaps in the ending of the central narrative of Pan and Iphigenia. It should serve as quite a good introduction to Greek mythology for school-age children who are just beginning to g</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText10362193172540232012">A bit of a tear-jerker, a bit of an Olympian love story, both of which should be obvious to anyone who already knows the related myths or the Greeks' penchant for classical tragedy. Napoli weaves a number of interrelated mytic stories into the tapestry, and in the process creates quite a plausible fill for two of the gaps in the ending of the central narrative of Pan and Iphigenia. It should serve as quite a good introduction to Greek mythology for school-age children who are just beginning to get a handle on this aspect of the roots of Western civilization and literature. The narrative form makes it much easier to digest than <a title="Edith Hamilton" href="https://www.goodreads.com/search/search?q=Edith%20Hamilton">Edith Hamilton</a> or <a title="Thomas Bulfinch" href="https://www.goodreads.com/search/search?q=Thomas%20Bulfinch">Thomas Bulfinch</a>, or any of the dry variety of what might be described as "mythological short stories" that so appeals to more adult academics.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer120755760">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11849441534047374190">Hotter than the Song of Solomon! Wow, the gods sure did get around. This is a beautiful book from cover to ending -- very romantic, and if you're not careful you might just learn something. This is slated as Y/A lit. Not sure my 10-year-old is ready for it, nor would he be interested in a romance between Pan and Iphegenia. It's more of a chick book (in a good way), and for a bit older -- I'd guess jr. high or older, depending on the person. Great summer read for me, though!</span>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer73024454">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6581537494746774247">A retelling of the Greek myths about Pan, both goat and god, whose reed flute frolicking leads him to a meeting with Iphigenia, a human raised as the daughter of King Agamemnon and Queen Clytemnestra.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked &amp;&amp; exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&amp;name=' + shelf_name + '&amp;a=' + action + '&amp;authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('A4bEM9vRtUdbsI5PLT02xCIGwcWxfOM5l+rNAySOYcZmUvvgKQOhvddo+vRTXNB2a/EC3PihpJP948iR6BuXgw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&amp;book_id=' + book_id + '&amp;refresh=true' + '&amp;authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('essSWRjkF60qCa3T3CzkiSVtLBktH27CtC7VR+o8e78fHy2K6jYDV6bR2WiiTQI7bJrvAGTCKWjeJ9DVJqmN+g==')})
  }
//]]&gt;
</script>

    <div class=" clearFloats bigBox" id="aboutAuthor"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/18684.Donna_Jo_Napoli">About Donna Jo Napoli</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
      <a href="/author/show/18684.Donna_Jo_Napoli"><img alt="18684" src="http://d.gr-assets.com/authors/1268450123p2/18684.jpg" class="right" /></a>
    <div class="readable">
      
<span id="freeTextContainer7006551925446497309">From her website:<br /><br />Donna Jo Napoli is both a linguist and a writer of children's and YA fiction. <br /><br />Donna Jo has five children. She dreams of moving to the woods and becoming a naturalist. She loves to garden and bake bread. <br /><br />At various times her house and yard have been filled with dogs, cats, birds, and rabbits. For thirteen years she had a cat named Taxi, and liked to go outside and call, "Taxi!" to</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText7006551925446497309">From her website:<br /><br />Donna Jo Napoli is both a linguist and a writer of children's and YA fiction. <br /><br />Donna Jo has five children. She dreams of moving to the woods and becoming a naturalist. She loves to garden and bake bread. <br /><br />At various times her house and yard have been filled with dogs, cats, birds, and rabbits. For thirteen years she had a cat named Taxi, and liked to go outside and call, "Taxi!" to make the neighbors wonder. But dear dear Taxi died in 2009.<br /><br />She lives outside Philadelphia. She received her BA in mathematics in 1970 and her Ph.D. in Romance Languages and Literatures in 1973, both from Harvard University, then did a postdoctoral year in Linguistics at MIT. She has since taught linguistics at Smith College, the University of North Carolina at Chapel Hill, Georgetown University, the University of Michigan at Ann Arbor, and Swarthmore College. It was at UM that she earned tenure (in 1981) and became a full professor (in 1984). She has held visiting positions at the University of Queensland (Australia), the University of Geneva (Switzerland), and Capital Normal University of Beijing (China), as well as lectured at the University of Sydney (Australia), Macquarie University (Australia), the University of the Witwatersrand (South Africa), and the University of Stellenbosch (South Africa). In the area of linguistics she has authored five books (one of which is being translated into Korean), co-authored four (one of which is in Italian), edited one, and co-edited four (with a fifth in press), ranging from theoretical linguistics to practical matters in language structure and use, including matters of interest to d/Deaf people. She has held grants and fellowships from the National Science Foundation, the National Endowment for the Humanities, the Mellon Foundation, and the Sloan Foundation.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="7006551925446497309">...more</a>
